NEC42 shares NEC's 9000/4500µs leader and 560µs pulse-distance bit encoding, so it is **distinguished purely by bit count** (42 vs 32) — `DecodeRaw` counts the NEC bit-pairs after the leader and routes a 42-bit frame to the NEC42 path, leaving the 32-bit NEC path untouched. The 42 bits (LSB-first) are address(13) + ~address(13) + command(8) + ~command(8); the two inverse fields are the checksum. **No confidently-wrong output**: reported as **NEC42** only when BOTH the 13-bit address-inverse and 8-bit command-inverse hold; a 42-bit frame whose inversions fail is surfaced as **NEC42ext** (26-bit address + 16-bit command, no inversion) rather than asserting a 13/8 split — exactly mirroring the Flipper firmware's interpret logic; the bit-count dispatch is guarded so a standard 32-bit NEC frame still decodes as NEC. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — a variable-length pulse-distance bit reader + the inverse-field checksum, stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**; extends existing tools so the **registry is unchanged** (an enhancement). The bit **layout is ported from the Flipper firmware's NEC `interpret`** (`*data & 0x1FFF`, `>>13`, `>>26`, `>>34`), verified by an **encode↔decode round-trip that reproduces the firmware's own NEC42 test values** (`test_nec42.irtest`: 0x1FFF/0xFF, 0x0AAA/0x55, …), an **independently hand-built 42-bit frame** decoding to the same address/command (proving the decoder reads the layout, not just that encode/decode are mutual inverses), the **NEC42ext** no-inversion path, a **32-bit-NEC-not-stolen** regression guard, and an out-of-range address rejection; fuzz-clean (NEC42 seeds added). `internal/ir`.
- `ir_raw_decode` + `ir_raw_encode` RCA protocol — ✅ v0.657.0 — **pivoted into the project's core IR/RF domain** (off the credential/TLS/email forensics run) by adding the **RCA** consumer-IR protocol (RCA-brand TVs / AV gear) to the raw-IR decoder + encoder, which covered NEC / NEC-extended / Samsung32 / Sony SIRC / Philips RC5 / Kaseikyo but not RCA. RCA is **24-bit pulse-distance** with a **distinct 4000µs/4000µs AGC leader** (so it dispatches cleanly with zero risk to the existing NEC/Samsung paths — gated by a tight ±350µs absolute tolerance because 4000µs falls inside Samsung's wide 4500±30% window) and a 500µs bit mark + 1000µs (0) / 2000µs (1) space; the frame is 4-bit address + 8-bit command + their two inverse fields. **No confidently-wrong output**: RCA is reported as such only when **BOTH** the 4-bit address-inverse and 8-bit command-inverse checksums hold; a frame failing either is surfaced **RCA-like / unverified** (raw fields, not asserted), and a non-RCA pulse train fails the leader gate or a bit match and is rejected. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — a pulse-distance bit reader + the inverse-field checksum, stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**; extends existing tools so the **registry is unchanged** (an enhancement, not a new tool). **Anchored to the Flipper firmware's own RCA decoder unit-test vector** (`applications/.../infrared/test_rca.irtest` → address **0x0F**, command **0x54**, hand-verified bit-for-bit) plus an `encodeRCA`∘`decodeRCA` **round-trip across the full 4-bit-address × 8-bit-command space**, a corrupted-inverse-field checksum-fail case, and a Samsung-not-misdispatched dispatch-isolation guard; fuzz-clean (RCA seeds added to the existing IR fuzz harnesses). The **RC6** Manchester variant (double-width toggle bit) was investigated this cycle and **deliberately deferred** — its toggle/merge handling needs a faithful port of the firmware's transition-based Manchester decoder + unambiguous one-frame-one-output vectors, a focused effort rather than a confidently-wrong partial decode. `internal/ir`.
- `email_auth_decode` (unified email-authentication record router) — ✅ shipped v0.656.0 — the **single entry point** over the email-auth triad (`spf_record_decode` + `dkim_record_decode` + `dmarc_record_decode`), the email-security analogue of the project's `secret_identify` / `hash_identify` routers. Paste **any** email-auth DNS TXT record and it **detects the kind and dispatches** to the matching decoder, so an operator (or an agent) pulling records from a bulk DNS dump / a config / a capture need not pre-classify them — the result names the detected `kind` and carries the full typed decode. Detection is by the record's **`v=` version tag** (the unambiguous discriminator SPF and DMARC both require, and DKIM uses when present); a DKIM key record that omits the optional `v=` is recognised by its `p=`/`k=` tags. **No confidently-wrong output**: routing is by the explicit version prefix (case-insensitive, dig-quote-tolerant), so an SPF record is **never** sent to the DKIM decoder; an unrecognised record (no `v=spf1`/`v=DMARC1`/`v=DKIM1` prefix and no DKIM `p=`/`k=` — e.g. an MTA-STS `v=STSv1` record) is **rejected, never guessed**; each underlying decoder keeps its own RFC-anchored validation. **Wrap-vs-native: native orchestration** over the already-shipped, independently spec-/oracle-anchored **and extended-fuzzed** decoders — **no new go.mod dep**, no new parsing logic, no new external trust. Verified by routing each of the three live record types to the correct kind + sub-result, DKIM-without-`v=`, case-insensitive `V=SPF1`, dig-quoted input, the SPF-not-misrouted-to-DKIM guard, and unrecognised-record rejection; fuzz-clean. (This fire also ran an **extended-fuzzing hardening pass** over the eight new session parsers — roca / sshpub / ja3×4 / dkim / dmarc / spf, ~60M executions total, **zero crashes** — confirming the surface this router builds on is robust.) `internal/emailauth`. Registry 637→638.
- `spf_record_decode` (SPF record static analysis) — ✅ shipped v0.655.0 — **completes the email-authentication triad** (`dkim_record_decode` + `dmarc_record_decode` + this). An SPF record (the `v=spf1 …` TXT record, RFC 7208) declares which hosts may send mail for a domain, so it is a direct read on **spoofability**. The headline findings are **objective and fall straight out of the record**: the terminal **`all` qualifier** sets the default disposition — `+all` authorises the **ENTIRE internet** to send as the domain (critical misconfiguration), `?all` neutral (no protection), `~all` softfail, `-all` fail (strict, recommended) — and the count of **DNS-lookup-causing mechanisms** (a/mx/ptr/exists/include + redirect) feeds the **RFC 7208 §4.6.4 limit of 10** (exceeding it is a permerror that makes SPF fail open). Decodes every mechanism (qualifier + type + value), the `redirect=` / `exp=` modifiers, flags the **deprecated `ptr`** mechanism (RFC 7208 §5.5), and warns on a missing terminal `all`, unreachable terms after `all`, and multiple `all`. **Scope / no confidently-wrong output**: this is **offline static analysis of one record** — the reported lookup count is the number of lookup terms **in this record** (a **lower bound**, stated explicitly: each `include`/`redirect` resolves to more, and the RFC limit is across the full resolved tree, which needs live DNS — never overclaimed); the `all` qualifier + mechanism structure are fully determined offline; `+all` is flagged critical because it **objectively** authorises all senders; a record not beginning with `v=spf1` is **rejected**; dig multi-string output (`"part1" "part2"`) is reconstructed per TXT concatenation semantics (verified by a split-mid-token vector). **Wrap-vs-native: native** — RFC 7208 term tokenising, stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**. **Pinned to live published records** via `dig` (google.com 1 include / `~all`; github.com 8 includes + ip4 / `~all`) plus `+all`-critical, all four qualifier meanings, ptr-deprecated, redirect, no-terminal-all, and not-SPF rejection coverage; fuzz-clean. This **closes out the offline email-auth triad** (SPF + DKIM + DMARC). `internal/spf`. Registry 636→637.
- `dmarc_record_decode` (DMARC policy DNS record forensics) — ✅ shipped v0.654.0 — the **enforcement-policy capstone of the email-auth triad** (after `dkim_record_decode`). A DMARC record (the `_dmarc.<domain>` TXT record, RFC 7489 §6.3) is the policy that ties **SPF and DKIM** together and tells receivers what to do with failing mail, so it is **the single best read on whether a domain can be spoofed**. The headline finding is **objective and falls straight out of the record**: `p=none` means the domain is **monitoring only and does NOT block spoofed mail** (the most common DMARC misconfiguration — looks protected but isn't), while `p=quarantine` / `p=reject` enforce. Decodes the requested **policy** (`p`), **subdomain policy** (`sp`), sampling **percent** (`pct`), **DKIM/SPF alignment** (`adkim`/`aspf`), failure-reporting options (`fo`), report interval (`ri`), and the **aggregate / forensic report destinations** (`rua`/`ruf` — useful OSINT for mapping a target's mail-security vendor). **No confidently-wrong output**: the **`enforcing` verdict is derived directly from `p`** (objective, not a guess — `quarantine`/`reject` → enforcing, `none`/missing → not); `pct<100` under an enforcing policy is flagged as **partial enforcement**; RFC 7489 defaults (`pct=100`, `adkim`/`aspf=r`, `ri=86400`) are surfaced explicitly; a record missing the required `p=` is surfaced **with a warning rather than a fabricated policy**; a record not beginning with `v=DMARC1` (e.g. an SPF record, or `p=` before `v=`) is **rejected**. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — RFC 7489 tag=value parsing, stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**. **Pinned to live published records** pulled via `dig` (google.com / paypal.com `p=reject`; github.com `p=quarantine; sp=reject; pct=100; rua/ruf; fo=1`) plus `p=none` monitoring, strict-alignment, partial-pct, missing-policy, default-value, and not-DMARC rejection coverage; fuzz-clean. Together with `dkim_record_decode` this covers two-thirds of the email-auth triad; **SPF** is the remaining follow-up (its true DNS-lookup count needs live resolution, so it ships with that caveat). `internal/dmarc`. Registry 635→636.
- `dkim_record_decode` (DKIM public-key DNS record forensics) — ✅ shipped v0.653.0 — **opens the email-authentication forensics surface** (a fresh domain, diversifying off the TLS-fingerprint run). A DKIM record (the `<selector>._domainkey.<domain>` TXT record, RFC 6376 / RFC 8463) is the **public half of a domain's mail-signing key**, and real anti-spoofing / IR / OSINT loot: the `p=` tag carries the key, so its **algorithm and size are directly readable** — and a **short RSA key is a classic, exploitable finding** (a 512/768-bit DKIM key can be **factored** and the domain's email **forged**, the well-documented 2012 mass-disclosure class). Decodes the **key type** (rsa / ed25519), **key size**, **hash algorithms** (`h=`), **service types** (`s=`), **flags** (`t=y` testing / `t=s` strict), notes (`n=`), and **revocation** (empty `p=`). **Two forensic levers**: the RSA **modulus** is surfaced (hex) so the key **chains straight into `roca_detect`** — a ROCA-vulnerable DKIM key is likewise forgeable — and the key size is flagged against the **RFC 8301 minimum** (sub-1024-bit → **WEAK / forgeable**, 1024-bit → advisory, 2048-bit recommended). **No confidently-wrong output**: the weak-key flags are **objective, RFC-anchored thresholds**, not subjective verdicts; a `p=` that does not parse as the declared key type is surfaced **with a warning rather than a fabricated size**; an empty `p=` is reported as **revoked**; a record with no `p=` is rejected as not-a-DKIM-key-record; DNS string folding (whitespace in `p=`) is stripped before decode. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — tag=value parsing + base64 + stdlib `crypto/x509` (SubjectPublicKeyInfo; PKCS#1 fallback), **no new go.mod dep**. **Pinned to openssl-generated records** (1024-bit → modulus `b71e36fc…`; 512-bit flagged **WEAK**) and the **RFC 8463 §3 Ed25519 published test vector** (`11qYAY…URo=` → 32-byte key, 256-bit); plus revocation / folded-key / default-key-type / testing-flag / malformed coverage; fuzz-clean. Pairs with `roca_detect` and `x509_certificate_decode`. **SPF and DMARC** policy records are the scoped follow-ups (the rest of the email-auth triad). `internal/dkim`. Registry 634→635.
- `ja4s_fingerprint` (JA4S TLS-server fingerprint from a captured ServerHello) — ✅ shipped v0.652.0 — the **server-side companion to `ja4_fingerprint`**, completing the JA4 client+server pair. Where JA4 fingerprints the *client*, JA4S fingerprints the **server's response** — which is how you fingerprint **C2 / malware server infrastructure**: a server's chosen cipher + extension set is distinctive, so pairing the client **JA4** with the server **JA4S** fingerprints **both ends of one handshake** (the strong threat-intel signal — a JA4+JA4S pair pins a specific client⇄server stack, the basis of FoxIO's malware-family database). Given the ServerHello bytes from a pcap (a full `0x16…` record or a bare `0x02…` handshake; hex with spaces / colons accepted) it returns the **JA4S** string, its three sections, the **raw `JA4S_r`**, and the negotiated TLS version / chosen cipher / ALPN. JA4S = `JA4S_a_JA4S_b_JA4S_c`: `a` = protocol + TLS version (read from the **ServerHello's** supported_versions) + extension count + chosen ALPN (**no SNI flag** — the server sends none); `b` = the server's **single chosen cipher**; `c` = first-12 of SHA-256 of the extension list **in ServerHello order**. Critically — and unlike client JA4 — **JA4S retains GREASE and does not sort** (transcribed from FoxIO's reference `to_ja4s`, which differs from `to_ja4`; getting this wrong would be a silent mis-fingerprint). **No confidently-wrong output**: full bounds-checking with a truncated capture **rejected**; a **ClientHello is detected and steered to `ja4_fingerprint`** rather than mis-fingerprinted; an extension-less ServerHello emits the spec's `000000000000`. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — a ServerHello wire walk + `crypto/sha256`, **sharing the `internal/ja3` parser** (the JA3/JA4 paths are unchanged and still green), stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**. **Pinned to the FoxIO reference test fixtures via the venv-oracle technique** — extracted the ServerHello bytes from FoxIO's own pcaps and asserted against **their published `JA4S` *and* raw `JA4S_r`**: a **TLS 1.0** ServerHello (`t100100_0005_bc98f8e001b5`, single ext `ff01`, no ALPN, legacy-version path) and a **TLS 1.3** ServerHello whose version is read from its **supported_versions** extension (`t130200_1301_234ea6891581`, exts `0033,002b` hashed in order). Plus ClientHello-rejection + malformed-input coverage; fuzz-clean (JA4SDecode harness). This **saturates the offline JA4 TLS pair** (client + server); JA4H needs HTTP, JA4L needs packet timing, JA4X needs the cert chain — separate primitives. `internal/ja3` (`ja4.go`). Registry 633→634.
- `ja4_fingerprint` (JA4 TLS-client fingerprint from a captured ClientHello) — ✅ shipped v0.651.0 — the **modern successor to JA3** (FoxIO), the immediate follow-up flagged when `ja3_fingerprint` shipped and now adopted by **CISA, Cloudflare, Zeek, and Wireshark**. JA4 is **more robust than JA3**: it **sorts** the cipher and extension lists, so a client that shuffles them (TLS 1.3 deliberately randomises extension order — which gives JA3 an unstable hash) still fingerprints to **one stable value**; and the fingerprint is **human-readable** — `t13d1516h2_…` already states TLS 1.3 / SNI present / 15 ciphers / 16 extensions / ALPN h2 before any hash pivot. Given the ClientHello bytes from a pcap (full `0x16…` record or bare `0x01…` handshake; hex with spaces / colons accepted) it returns the **JA4** string, its three sections, the **raw `JA4_r`** (un-hashed, for auditing), and the parsed TLS version / SNI / ALPN. JA4 = `JA4_a_JA4_b_JA4_c`: `a` = protocol + TLS version (read from **supported_versions**, highest non-GREASE) + SNI flag (d/i) + cipher / extension counts + first-ALPN; `b` = first-12 of SHA-256 of the **sorted** cipher list; `c` = first-12 of SHA-256 of the **sorted** extension list (**SNI 0x0000 + ALPN 0x0010 excluded** — the consistency trick) then `_` + the **signature_algorithms in original order**. **GREASE (RFC 8701) removed** throughout. **No confidently-wrong output**: the bytes are walked with full bounds-checking and a truncated / malformed capture is **rejected**; a **ServerHello is detected and reported** (JA4S is a separate primitive) rather than mis-fingerprinted; the empty-extension case emits the spec's `000000000000`. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — the JA4 computation **shares the just-shipped `internal/ja3` ClientHello parser** (refactored to a common `Hello` walk; the JA3 path is unchanged and still green) + `crypto/sha256`, stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**. **Pinned to the FoxIO reference test fixtures via the venv-oracle technique** — extracted the ClientHello bytes from FoxIO's own pcaps and asserted against **their published `JA4` *and* raw `JA4_r` expected values**: a TLS 1.3 hello with GREASE / SNI / ALPN h2 / sig-algs (`t13d1516h2_8daaf6152771_e5627efa2ab1`, every sorted cipher/extension/sig-alg in the raw form matching byte-for-byte) and a TLS 1.0 hello exercising the **legacy-version path + empty-JA4_c** (`t10d230100_6a57a6f57151_000000000000`); each extracted hello was independently cross-checked by confirming its sorted cipher list reproduces FoxIO's `JA4_r`. Plus unit coverage of the version-label map, the ALPN first/last-alnum encoding (h2 / http1.1→h1 / absent→00), and ServerHello / malformed rejection; fuzz-clean (JA4Decode harness). **JA4S** (server-side) and the **JA4+ suite** (JA4H/JA4L/JA4X) are scoped follow-ups. `internal/ja3` (`ja4.go`). Registry 632→633.
- `ja3_fingerprint` (JA3 TLS-client fingerprint from a captured ClientHello) — ✅ shipped v0.650.0 — **opens the network / TLS threat-intel surface**, a fresh domain that complements the Marauder / WiFi capture tooling and the credential-forensics decoders. **JA3** (Salesforce) is the fingerprint format wired into **Suricata, Zeek, and every major EDR / threat-intel feed**: it identifies a TLS client stack — and frequently the **malware family** behind it — **independent of IP or SNI**, so a beaconing implant that rotates infrastructure still hashes to the **same JA3**. Given the **ClientHello** bytes pulled from a pcap (a full `0x16…` TLS record or a bare `0x01…` handshake; hex with spaces / colons accepted), it returns the **JA3 string** + its **MD5 digest** — ready to pivot against a JA3 blocklist / feed — plus the parsed offered ciphers, extensions, curves, point formats, and SNI. JA3 concatenates `SSLVersion,Cipher,SSLExtension,EllipticCurve,EllipticCurvePointFormat` (values dash-joined) and MD5s it, with **GREASE values (RFC 8701) removed** from the cipher / extension / curve lists so a client randomising GREASE still yields one stable hash. **No confidently-wrong output**: the bytes are walked with full bounds-checking and a truncated / malformed capture is **rejected** rather than half-fingerprinted; a **ServerHello (handshake type 2) is detected and reported as JA3S-not-yet-supported** rather than mis-fingerprinted. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — a ClientHello wire walk (RFC 5246 §7.4.1.2) + `crypto/md5`, stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**. **Pinned to the Salesforce reference implementation (pyja3) via the project's venv-oracle technique** — a real `openssl s_client` ClientHello reproduces pyja3's exact JA3 string + digest (`0b85eb0d4981e69064e40753e4f0ac5f`), and a **hand-built GREASE-bearing ClientHello** reproduces pyja3's GREASE-stripped output (`771,4865-4866-49199-47,0-10-11,29-23,0`, exercising the high-risk filtering path) — plus the **two string→MD5 worked examples from the JA3 spec** pin the hashing step (`ada70206…`, `de350869…`). Fuzz-clean (Decode + FromClientHello harnesses). **JA3S** (server-side ServerHello variant — fields `SSLVersion,Cipher,SSLExtension`) is a scoped, clearly-flagged follow-up; **JA4** (the newer FoxIO sorted-list fingerprint) is a separate future primitive. `internal/ja3`. Registry 631→632.
- `ssh_pubkey_decode` (OpenSSH public-key / authorized_keys / known_hosts triage) — ✅ shipped v0.649.0 — fills a real gap on the credential-loot surface: the project decoded OpenSSH **private** keys (`ssh_privkey_decode`), PEM private keys (`pem_privkey_decode`), and PuTTY `.ppk` (`putty_privkey_decode`), but nothing triaged the **public**-key artifacts an operator actually finds first — an `authorized_keys` file on a compromised host, or a `known_hosts` file that maps the box's **lateral-movement reach**. Paste one line or a whole file and get, per key: the **type** (ssh-ed25519 / ssh-rsa / ecdsa-sha2-nistp256/384/521 / ssh-dss / `sk-…` FIDO security keys), the **key size**, the **SHA256 and MD5 fingerprints exactly as `ssh-keygen -l` prints them**, the **comment**, any `authorized_keys` **options**, and any `known_hosts` **marker** (`@cert-authority` / `@revoked`) + host field. Two forensic levers beyond parsing: (1) for an **ssh-rsa** key the **modulus** is surfaced in hex so the key **chains straight into `roca_detect`** — fingerprint the key, then screen the RSA ones for the Infineon **ROCA** weakness (CVE-2017-15361); a sub-2048-bit RSA key is flagged weak; (2) for a **hashed `known_hosts` entry** (`|1|salt|hash`) supplying a candidate **hostname** tests it against the **HMAC-SHA1**, **deanonymising** which host the entry refers to (the `ssh-keygen -F` technique, the standard way to read a hashed known_hosts file) — plaintext host lists are matched directly (comma lists + `*`/`?` globs). **No confidently-wrong output**: a key blob is accepted **only** when its **embedded algorithm name matches its declared type** (the validity gate — a corrupted or mislabelled blob is rejected, not mis-decoded); a malformed line is surfaced with a note rather than aborting the batch; a non-matching candidate hostname is reported as no match, never guessed. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — the public-key wire blob is parsed directly off the **RFC 4253** length-prefixed format and fingerprinted with stdlib `crypto/sha256` + `crypto/md5`; the hashed-host test is stdlib `crypto/hmac` + `crypto/sha1`. **No `x/crypto/ssh` surface** (and so none of its govulncheck advisories) and **no new go.mod dep**. **Pinned byte-for-byte to `ssh-keygen -l` / `-H` / `-F`**: freshly generated **ed25519 / rsa-2048 / ecdsa-nistp256 / ssh-dss** keys reproduce its exact SHA256 (and MD5) fingerprints + key sizes (256/2048/256/1024), and the hashed-host vector (`|1|nfJ9…|4eDWZz…`) deanonymises to `server1.example.com` while a different host correctly does not match. Fuzz-clean. Pairs with `roca_detect`, `ssh_privkey_decode`, and `ssh_handshake_decode`. `internal/sshpub`. Registry 630→631.
- `roca_detect` (ROCA / CVE-2017-15361 weak-RSA-key detector) — ✅ shipped v0.648.0 — opens the **key-material vulnerability-audit** surface alongside the credential-forensics tools: given only an RSA **public** key, flags whether its **private** key is practically **factorable** because it was generated by the Infineon **RSALib** (the ROCA flaw, CVE-2017-15361). The affected hardware is exactly the kind a pentester / IR analyst meets in the field — **Yubikey 4/Neo**, Infineon **TPMs**, **Gemalto IDPrime** smartcards, and the **Estonian / Slovak national eID** cards — and the Coppersmith attack of Nemec et al. (CCS 2017) recovers the secret key from the public modulus alone, so being able to screen a cert / SSH key / smartcard key **offline, with no factorisation and no network**, is the whole point. Accepts a bare RSA **modulus** (decimal or `0x`-hex), a **PEM public key** (PKIX/SPKI or PKCS#1), a PEM **X.509 certificate**, or an OpenSSH **ssh-rsa** authorized_key line; extracts the modulus and runs the published fingerprint test (for each of 38 small primes the residue `modulus mod pᵢ` must fall in a precomputed marker bitmask — the Infineon generator forces it into a small subgroup). **No confidently-wrong output**: the fingerprint **never clears a vulnerable key** (a negative is reliable), and a positive is reported as a **near-certain hit, confirmed only by the full factorisation** — surfaced in the note, not overclaimed; the markers carry a negligible-but-nonzero false-positive rate, stated rather than hidden. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — the 38 primes + 38 marker bitmasks are ported **verbatim** from the reference tool **crocs-muni/roca** (`roca/detect.py`, `has_fingerprint_moduli`), evaluated with `math/big` bit operations (the markers exceed 64 bits); `crypto/x509` + `encoding/pem` are stdlib and the **ssh-rsa key is parsed natively** off the RFC 4253 length-prefixed wire format, so the `x/crypto/ssh` surface (and its govulncheck advisories) is **not** pulled in and there is **no new go.mod dep**. **Validated against that project's ten fingerprint-positive test moduli** (`tests/test_fingerprint.py` `test_fake_mods`) — all ten flag vulnerable, which also confirms the constant transcription (a single wrong digit shifts the residues mod the 38 primes and the fingerprint stops matching) — plus a false-positive guard that generates fresh `crypto/rsa` 2048-bit keys (a sound, non-Infineon library) and asserts none are flagged, decimal-vs-hex equivalence, PKIX / PKCS#1 / certificate / ssh-rsa input paths, and empty / malformed / non-key rejections. Fuzz-clean. Pairs with `secret_identify` and the PGP / keystore forensics tools. `internal/roca`. Registry 629→630.
- `discord_token_decode` (Discord token → owning account) — ✅ shipped v0.647.0 — decodes the **single most common credential in infostealer / RAT logs** (RedLine, Raccoon, et al. harvest Discord tokens en masse) into the **account it belongs to**. A captured Discord user/bot token is **not opaque**: its first `.`-separated segment is `base64url(user-ID)`, and that snowflake yields the **account creation time** — so identifying the owning account + its age **offline, with no API call to Discord, no token use, no detection** is standard IR / OSINT triage. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — a Base64 decode + the in-tree `snowflake_decode` (already anchored to Discord's documented example `175928847299117063` → 2016-04-30T11:18:25.796Z), stdlib + an existing package, **no new go.mod dep**. **No confidently-wrong output**: the **token mint timestamp** (segment 2) is surfaced **raw and uninterpreted** — Discord's epoch offset for it is documented as uncertain ("add 1.1e9-1.3e9"), so converting it to a date would be a guess; the HMAC (segment 3) is opaque; an `mfa.`-prefixed token (no embedded user ID) is identified as such; a string whose first segment doesn't decode to ASCII digits (e.g. a JWT, whose header is JSON) is **rejected**. Verified by a round-trip from the documented snowflake (token → user ID `175928847299117063` → 2016-04-30 creation), a standard-Base64 segment case, MFA-token identification, and JWT-like / no-dots / non-digit rejections; fuzz-clean. **Also wired into `secret_identify`** (a Discord token now classifies as `token-discord` with the user ID + creation time, after the JWT check). `internal/discordtoken`. Registry 628→629.
- `secret_identify` (credential / secret triage front end) — ✅ shipped v0.646.0 — the **unified entry point** for the credential-forensics tooling, the analogue of `hash_identify` for tokens/keys: paste an unknown string pulled from a repo / config / `.env` / log / memory capture and get the **type** — and, where the format carries a checksum or structure, **whether it validates**. It **routes to the in-tree decoders** (`aws_key_decode` → account ID, `github_token_decode` → CRC32 checksum, `azure_sas_decode`, `bip39_decode` → SHA-256 checksum, `jwt_decode` → alg) for the validated formats, detects PGP / OpenSSH / PEM private keys + X.509 certificates **by structure**, and recognises a curated set of vendor tokens **by documented prefix** (Slack, GitLab, Stripe, npm, OpenAI / Anthropic, Google, SendGrid, DigitalOcean, Shopify, Azure connection strings, …). **No confidently-wrong output**: a result asserts the **format** (and its validity *only* where a checksum/structure was actually checked — `validated:true`), never that a credential is live; a prefix-only match is `validated:false`; the `sk-`/`sk_live_` ambiguity is resolved by prefix ordering; an unrecognised string is returned **unmatched with a shape hint** (hex / base64 / "try hash_identify") rather than guessed. **Wrap-vs-native: native orchestration** over the already-shipped, reference-anchored decoders + a documented vendor-prefix table — **no new go.mod dep**, no new external trust. Verified across every detection path (AWS published vector → account `609629065308`, the GitHub canonical token, JWT alg, Azure SAS, the five PEM variants, nine vendor prefixes, the all-`abandon`/`about` BIP-39 mnemonic, and unmatched shape-hints), with the Stripe-vs-OpenAI prefix-ordering guarded by a dedicated test; fuzz-clean. `internal/secretid`. Registry 627→628.
- `github_token_decode` (GitHub token identifier + checksum validator) — ✅ shipped v0.645.0 — broadens the credential-forensics surface to **secret-scanning / leak triage**: identifies and **validates a GitHub authentication token** — the prefixed, checksummed formats GitHub adopted April 2021 (`ghp_` PAT classic, `gho_` OAuth, `ghu_` user-to-server, `ghs_` server-to-server, `ghr_` refresh, `github_pat_` fine-grained). A leaked GitHub token is the **single most common secret** found in repos / dumps / logs / CI configs, and the format carries a **CRC32 checksum** that confirms **offline — with no API call to GitHub** — whether a captured string is a **genuine, well-formed token** vs. a redaction / typo / fabricated lookalike (a positive secret-scanning detection from the token alone). For the five classic types it reports the kind + checksum validity; a fine-grained `github_pat_` is identified by prefix but its checksum is **not asserted** (its internal structure differs and is not vector-verified here). **No confidently-wrong output**: a token whose checksum doesn't validate is reported as such (not asserted genuine); an unrecognised prefix or non-Base62 body is rejected. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — a `hash/crc32` over the post-prefix entropy compared to the Base62-decoded last-6 checksum (Base62 dict `0-9A-Za-z`), stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**. **Verified against the canonical example token** (prefix `ghp_`, entropy `zQWBuTSOoRi4A9spHcVY5ncnsDkxkJ`, checksum `0mLq17`) — its entropy's CRC32 (714468973) equals the Base62-decoded checksum, confirming both the algorithm and the vector — plus a corrupted-checksum-flagged case, all five classic prefixes validating under the same algorithm, fine-grained identification, and unknown-prefix / too-short / non-GitHub rejections; fuzz-clean. (A GitHub-token validator was **deferred** the prior cycle for lack of a confident vector; this cycle the canonical example was confirmed checksum-valid, unblocking it.) `internal/githubtoken`. Registry 626→627.
- `azure_sas_decode` (Azure Storage SAS token decoder) — ✅ shipped v0.644.0 — the **Azure companion to `aws_key_decode`** in the cloud-credential forensics surface: decodes an Azure Storage **Shared Access Signature** (the `?sv=…&sp=…&se=…&sig=…` query string that delegates access to Blob / Queue / Table / File storage) into its **blast radius** — the SAS type (service / account / user-delegation), the granted **permissions expanded to human operations**, the **validity window** (start / expiry), the **scope** (services / resource types / resource), the allowed **IP range** + **protocol**, and any stored-access-policy reference. A leaked SAS token (in a URL, a config, a log, a repo) is real cloud-IR / pentest loot, and the first question is always *what can this token do, and until when?* — answered **offline**. Accepts a full URL or a bare query string. The HMAC **signature can't be verified without the account key**, so it is reported present-but-opaque. **No confidently-wrong output**: permission letters are **context-dependent** (`p` = Permissions/ACL on a blob but Process on a queue; `r` = Read on a blob but **Query** on a table), so they are expanded against the resource context derived from `sr` / `ss` / `tn` — when the context isn't definite (account SAS, or a context-free token) the common Blob meaning is shown **with a caveat note**, and an unknown letter is surfaced raw; a string with no SAS fields is rejected. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — `net/url` query parse + the documented Azure SAS field-code tables, stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**. **Anchored to the Microsoft Azure Storage SAS reference** — its worked example `sp=rw&st=…&se=…&sip=…&spr=https&sv=…&sr=b` decodes to Read+Write on a Blob with the exact window / IP / protocol — plus account-SAS (`ss`/`srt` expansion + caveat), table-context (`r = Query`), and user-delegation (`skoid`/`sktid`) cases, and no-SAS-fields / bad-query rejections; fuzz-clean. `internal/azuresas`. Registry 625→626.
- `aws_key_decode` (AWS access key ID → account ID decoder) — ✅ shipped v0.643.0 — opens the **cloud-credential forensics** surface: recovers the **AWS account ID** that is bit-packed inside an access key ID (`AKIA…` / `ASIA…` / `AROA…` and the other 20-char AWS unique IDs) plus the **credential type**, entirely **offline — no `sts:GetAccessKeyInfo` call, no CloudTrail entry, no detection**. A leaked AWS key is prime cloud-pentest / IR loot, and scoping it to an owning account (and knowing whether it is a usable access key vs. a resource unique ID) is standard recon. Identifies the type from the prefix (AKIA = long-term IAM key, ASIA = temporary STS key, AROA = role, AIDA = user, ANPA = managed policy, …) and flags `usable_credential` for AKIA/ASIA. **No confidently-wrong output**: only the recognised AWS unique-ID prefixes are accepted — a wrong length, an unknown prefix, or a non-base32 body is **rejected** rather than decoded into a bogus account ID. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — strip the 4-char prefix, base32-decode the body, read the first 6 bytes big-endian, mask `0x7FFFFFFFFF80`, right-shift 7 (the layout reverse-engineered by Aidan Steele / WithSecure / Truffle Security); a base32 decode + a shift, stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**. **Anchored byte-for-byte to two published vectors** — `ASIAY34FZKBOKMUTVV7A` → `609629065308` and `ASIAQNZGKIQY56JQ7WML` → `029608264753` (the latter is the `psanford/aws-account-id-from-key` reference implementation's own test vector) — plus case-insensitivity, per-prefix type identification, and wrong-length / unknown-prefix / non-base32 rejections; fuzz-clean (~1.5M execs, 0 crashes). `internal/awskey`. Registry 624→625.
- `pgp_packet_decode` signature subpackets — ✅ v0.642.0 — extended `pgp_packet_decode` with **signature subpacket parsing** (RFC 4880 §5.2.3), surfacing the fields that make a signature forensically useful: **signature creation time**, **issuer key ID + issuer fingerprint** (which key signed it — the pivot that links a signature back to a key), **key / signature expiry**, and **key flags** (certify / sign / encrypt / authenticate). Walks both the hashed and unhashed subpacket areas (v4/v5 + the v3 inline form). **Verified by cross-checking against `x/crypto/openpgp`'s parsed `packet.Signature`** (the same test oracle): every decoded signature's creation time + issuer key ID must match the reference implementation's `.CreationTime` / `.IssuerKeyId`. Still **native** (a TLV subpacket walk, stdlib only — the runtime depends on none of `x/crypto/openpgp`); fuzz-clean. No new tool — extends `pgp_packet_decode` (`internal/pgppacket`); registry unchanged. (A separate `ssh_key_decrypt` was investigated this cycle and **deferred**: decrypting an encrypted OpenSSH key needs `x/crypto/ssh`'s bcrypt-pbkdf, whose only fix for GO-2026-5018 is an x/crypto v0.50→v0.52 bump that cascades across five `golang.org/x/` modules — left to Renovate rather than forced mid-feature.)
- `pgp_packet_decode` (OpenPGP key/message packet decoder) — ✅ shipped v0.641.0 — opens the **PGP / OpenPGP credential-forensics** surface (a fresh domain alongside the JWT / Kerberos / NTLM / hash credential tooling): walks the **RFC 4880 / RFC 9580 packet stream** of a captured PGP key or message (a `.asc` / `.gpg` file, an armored block from an email or a key dump) into a structured per-packet view — tag + length, and for key packets the **version, algorithm, creation time, fingerprint, and 64-bit key ID**. Identifying a key's fingerprint/key ID, its algorithm + creation time, and the user IDs it certifies is standard triage, and **a secret-key packet is the private key itself**. Accepts ASCII-armor (`-----BEGIN PGP …`), base64, hex, or raw binary. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — the packet framing (old/new-format headers, partial lengths), the v4/v5 fingerprint formula (RFC 4880 §12.2: SHA-1 over `0x99 ‖ len ‖ body`, SHA-256 over `0x9A ‖ …` for v5), the MPI layout, and the tag/algorithm tables are a public spec — a TLV walker + a hash, stdlib only; **the runtime depends on none of `golang.org/x/crypto/openpgp`** (deprecated/frozen), which is used **only as the test oracle**. **No confidently-wrong output**: a public-key fingerprint hashes the whole body (correct for every algorithm); a secret-key fingerprint isolates the public portion by walking the public MPIs for **RSA / DSA / Elgamal**, while an **ECC secret key's fingerprint is flagged rather than guessed** (its OID/point layout is not oracle-cross-checked); a truncated / overrunning packet length stops the walk with a warning rather than panicking; non-OpenPGP input is rejected; v3 (legacy MD5) fingerprints are surfaced-but-not-computed. **Verified by cross-checking the native walker against the x/crypto reference implementation** on a freshly generated entity — every fingerprint / key ID / creation time / tag matches byte-for-byte for the **public** key (`Serialize`) and the **secret** key (`SerializePrivate`, proving the public-MPI isolation), plus an **independent hand-computed SHA-1 fingerprint for a non-RSA (EdDSA) public key** the RSA-only oracle cannot generate, an armored-vs-binary equivalence check, and non-OpenPGP rejections. Fuzz-clean (~1.5M execs, 0 crashes). `internal/pgppacket`. Registry 623→624.
- `eth_keystore_decrypt` (Ethereum V3 keystore decryptor) — ✅ shipped v0.640.0 — extends crypto-wallet forensics to **Ethereum**: decrypts the encrypted JSON wallet file that **Geth / MyEtherWallet / MetaMask** and most Ethereum tooling export (the `UTC--…` / keystore file), recovering the **32-byte private key** with the operator's passphrase. A captured keystore is prime IR / pentest loot — an offline-crackable wrapper around an ETH private key, the Ethereum counterpart to a BIP-39 seed (`bip39_decode`) or a WIF key (`base58check_decode`). Handles the Web3 Secret Storage scheme: **scrypt** or **PBKDF2-HMAC-SHA256** KDF, **AES-128-CTR**, and a **Keccak-256 MAC**. **No confidently-wrong output**: the MAC is the gate — `Keccak-256(derivedKey[16:32] ‖ ciphertext)` must equal the stored MAC; when it does not (wrong passphrase / corrupt file) the private key is **NOT surfaced** (`mac_valid:false` + a note). A **hostile scrypt N** (128·N·r over 1 GiB) or an out-of-range PBKDF2 iteration count is **rejected** rather than allowed to exhaust the host; an unsupported cipher/KDF or malformed JSON is rejected. **Wrap-vs-native: native orchestration** — scrypt/Keccak from `golang.org/x/crypto` (already a dependency) + stdlib AES/CTR + our own JSON parse / MAC gate / field assembly; **no new go.mod dep**, no shell-out. Address derivation (private key → address) needs secp256k1 (not a current dependency) and is deliberately deferred — the recovered key is the loot, importable into any wallet. **Anchored byte-for-byte to the canonical Web3 Secret Storage PBKDF2 test vector** — passphrase "testpassword" → private key `7a28b5ba57c53603b0b07b56bba752f7784bf506fa95edc395f5cf6c7514fe9d` (the documented secret, decrypted exactly; verification caught a mistranscribed MAC in my own draft vector before shipping) — plus a scrypt encrypt∘decrypt round-trip, wrong-passphrase MAC-gating (no key surfaced), and unsupported-cipher / unsupported-KDF / hostile-scrypt-N / malformed-JSON rejections. Fuzz-clean (~4.3M execs, 0 crashes). `internal/ethkeystore`. Registry 622→623.
- `bech32_decode` (Bech32 / Bech32m SegWit-address / Nostr / Lightning decoder) — ✅ shipped v0.639.0 — the **Bech32 companion to `base58check_decode`**, closing out Bitcoin-address coverage (Base58Check legacy `1…`/`3…` + WIF, now Bech32 `bc1…`). Bech32/Bech32m (BIP-173 / BIP-350) is the encoding modern Bitcoin uses for **SegWit addresses**, and which **Nostr** (`npub`/`nsec`/`note`), **Lightning** (`lnbc…`), and Cosmos-family chains also use. Reports the HRP, the **checksum variant** (bech32 vs bech32m) + validity, and the 5→8-bit data payload (hex). For the SegWit HRPs (bc/tb/bcrt) it decodes the **witness version** + **witness program** and identifies **P2WPKH** / **P2WSH** / **P2TR (Taproot)**, **enforcing the BIP-173/350 rule** that witness v0 uses Bech32 and v1+ uses Bech32m (a mismatch is flagged). Nostr / Lightning HRPs are labelled (their inner TLV / invoice structure left to the caller). **No confidently-wrong output**: a non-validating checksum, or a SegWit address whose variant does not match its witness version, is reported rather than asserted valid; mixed-case input, a missing `1` separator, or an out-of-charset character is rejected. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — base-32 charset + the BCH checksum polynomial + a 5↔8-bit regroup, stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**. **Anchored to the BIP-173 / BIP-350 test vectors** — `A12UEL5L` (Bech32, HRP "a"), `A1LQFN3A` (Bech32m, HRP "a"), and the canonical P2WPKH `bc1qw508d6qejxtdg4y5r3zarvary0c5xw7kv8f3t4` → witness v0 / program `751e76e8199196d454941c45d1b3a323f1433bd6` — plus an independent encoder round-trip for a v1/Taproot (Bech32m) address, a wrong-variant-flagged case, a Nostr `npub` label+payload case, and bad-checksum / mixed-case / no-separator / bad-char rejections. Fuzz-clean (~5.8M execs, 0 crashes). `internal/bech32`. Registry 621→622.
- `base58check_decode` (WIF / address / xprv Base58Check decoder) — ✅ shipped v0.638.0 — the **Base58Check companion to `bip39_decode`**, extending the crypto-wallet forensics surface from seed phrases to the encoded key/address artifacts. Base58Check is the encoding Bitcoin (and many forks) use for **WIF private keys**, **legacy addresses**, and **BIP-32 extended keys** — a leaked WIF key, address, or xprv/xpub is common IR / pentest loot. Decodes the version + payload, validates the **4-byte double-SHA-256 checksum**, and identifies the artifact: **P2PKH** (0x00 mainnet / 0x6F testnet), **P2SH** (0x05 / 0xC4), **WIF private keys** (0x80 / 0xEF — surfacing the 32-byte private key + the compressed flag), and field-parses **BIP-32 extended keys** (xprv/xpub/tprv/tpub: depth, parent fingerprint, child number, chain code, key) from the fixed 78-byte body. **No confidently-wrong output**: a string whose checksum does not validate is reported as such (likely a typo / truncation) rather than asserted genuine; an unknown version byte is surfaced raw; a non-Base58 character or a too-short decode is rejected. Bech32 (segwit `bc1…`) is a different encoding and deliberately out of scope (a separate decoder). **Wrap-vs-native: native** — base-58 (`math/big`) + double-SHA-256 + version prefix, stdlib only, **no new go.mod dep**. **Anchored byte-for-byte to the canonical Bitcoin vectors** — the WIF `5HueCGU8rMjxEXxiPuD5BDku4MkFqeZyd4dZ1jvhTVqvbTLvyTJ` → private key `0c28fca3…72aa1d` (uncompressed, mainnet), and the genesis address `1A1zP1eP5QGefi2DMPTfTL5SLmv7DivfNa` → hash160 `62e907b1…88f18` — plus an independent Base58Check-encoder round-trip over P2SH / testnet-WIF / compressed-WIF / xprv (with field parse), a bad-checksum-flagged case, and non-Base58 / too-short rejections. Fuzz-clean (~830K execs, 0 crashes). `internal/base58check`. Registry 620→621.
- `bip39_decode` (BIP-39 wallet seed-phrase decoder/validator) — ✅ shipped v0.637.0 — opens the **crypto-wallet forensics** surface: validates a **BIP-39 mnemonic** (the 12/15/18/21/24-word seed phrase every Bitcoin/Ethereum/hardware wallet uses) and derives its seed. A captured seed phrase is the root secret from which every wallet key descends, so confirming a phrase is a **genuine** mnemonic (vs. a typo / wrong word / wrong order) and deriving its seed is prime IR / pentest loot. Returns `entropy_hex`, `entropy_bits` (128-256), `checksum_valid`, the per-word list `indices`, and the 64-byte `seed_hex` (PBKDF2-HMAC-SHA512(mnemonic, 'mnemonic'+passphrase, 2048), with the optional BIP-39 passphrase / 25th word). **No confidently-wrong output**: a phrase whose **SHA-256 checksum does not validate** is reported as such (likely a typo) rather than asserted genuine — the seed is still derived from the words as given but clearly flagged; a non-wordlist word or an invalid word count is **rejected**. Case- and whitespace-insensitive. **English wordlist only** (the embedded official BIP-39 list, SHA-256 `2f5eed53…3b24dbda`); other languages are rejected, not guessed. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — 11-bit word-index unpacking + SHA-256 checksum + PBKDF2-HMAC-SHA512 over the embedded 2048-word list, stdlib crypto + the in-tree `wpa.PBKDF2`; **no new runtime dep** (x/text's NFKD normaliser was already an indirect module dependency, now direct). **Anchored byte-for-byte to the official Trezor BIP-39 test vectors** — the all-`abandon … about` mnemonic → entropy `00000000000000000000000000000000` and (passphrase "TREZOR") seed `c55257c3…7463b04`, and `legal winner thank year … yellow` → entropy `7f7f…7f` / seed `2e890581…ce1f607` — plus an independent encoder round-trip across all five lengths (128/160/192/224/256-bit), a bad-checksum-flagged case, and case/whitespace/word-count/non-wordlist rejections. Fuzz-clean (~1.7M execs, 0 crashes). BIP-32 master-key / address derivation from the seed is deliberately left to the caller (`internal/bip39`). Registry 619→620.
- `otpauth_migration_decode` (Google Authenticator export decoder) — ✅ shipped v0.636.0 — **bulk-recovers every 2FA secret from a Google Authenticator export QR**, the high-value complement to `totp_generate` (which takes a single seed). Authenticator's *Export accounts* / *Transfer accounts* QR is an `otpauth-migration://offline?data=…` URI whose `data` is a base64 **protobuf** (`MigrationPayload`) packing **all** of a user's seeds — so one captured export QR / screenshot / deep-link yields every second factor at once (a real post-exploitation / device-forensics step). Decodes each account's issuer, name, **base32 secret**, algorithm (SHA1/256/512), digits, type (totp/hotp), HOTP counter, **and a reconstructed `otpauth://` URI ready to paste straight into `totp_generate`** for the live codes. Accepts the full URI or the bare base64 (std/URL/padded/unpadded). **No confidently-wrong output**: an unknown algorithm/digit/type enum value is surfaced raw (`UNSPECIFIED(n)`); a single `otpauth://` URI (not a migration export), a non-base64 payload, or a payload carrying no accounts is **rejected**. **Wrap-vs-native: native** — the public-schema protobuf is parsed directly with `google.golang.org/protobuf/encoding/protowire` (already a module dependency, used as a low-level varint/bytes reader; **no generated `.pb.go`, no new `go.mod` entry**) + stdlib base64/base32; nothing wrapped or shelled out. **Verified** by a protowire-encoder round-trip over single / multi-account / 8-digit-SHA256 / HOTP-with-counter payloads, an unknown-enum surfacing case, URI / non-base64 / no-account rejections, and — the external anchor — the **secret cross-checked against the independently hand-computed base32** of the canonical `Hello!`+`0xDEADBEEF` example: **JBSWY3DPEHPK3PXP**. Fuzz-clean (~3.9M execs, 0 crashes). Pairs with `totp_generate` and the credential tooling (`internal/otpmigration`). Registry 618→619.
- `ksuid_decode` (KSUID timestamp + payload decoder) — ✅ shipped v0.635.0 — **extends the identifier info-leak family** (`uuid_decode` / `objectid_decode` / `ulid_decode` / `snowflake_decode`) with **KSUID** — the K-Sortable Unique IDentifier (segmentio/ksuid) used widely by Go backends. A KSUID is a 27-char base62 string encoding 20 bytes: a 4-byte big-endian timestamp (seconds since a custom 2014 epoch) + 16 bytes of randomness. Like a UUIDv1/v7, ObjectId, ULID or Snowflake it is **not opaque** — its leading bytes leak the creation time of whatever it identifies (request IDs, tokens, DB keys, URLs, logs), and its lexicographic sortability aids enumeration. Decodes the **UTC creation timestamp** + unix seconds, the raw 32-bit timestamp field, and the 16-byte payload (hex). Unlike a Snowflake, a KSUID is **unambiguous** (one published format, one epoch), so the timestamp is a single asserted answer. **No confidently-wrong output**: a wrong length, an out-of-alphabet character, or a 160-bit value that overflows 20 bytes is **rejected**, not mis-decoded. **Anchored byte-for-byte to segmentio/ksuid's own documented example** — `0ujtsYcgvSTl8PAuAdqWYSMnLOv` → raw `0669F7EFB5A1CD34B5F99D1154FB6853345C9735`, timestamp field `0x0669F7EF` (107608047) + epoch → 2017-10-10T04:00:47Z, payload `B5A1CD34B5F99D1154FB6853345C9735` — plus the documented nil (all-zero → the 2014 epoch) and max (`aWgEPTl1tmebfsQzFP4bxwgy80V` → all-FF) KSUIDs and overflow / bad-char / bad-length rejections; fuzz-clean (~750K execs, 0 crashes). Native — base62 decode (`math/big`) + a big-endian read + an epoch add, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/ksuid`). Registry 617→618.
- `subghz_pocsag_decode` BCH(31,21,2) error correction — ✅ shipped v0.634.0 — hardened the shipped POCSAG paging decoder (rank #4) so a **noisy over-the-air capture decodes correctly instead of silently wrong**. The decoder previously only *checked* even parity; it now applies **maximum-likelihood BCH(31,21,2) correction** — up to two bit errors per 32-bit codeword are repaired before the address / message bits are extracted. Because the code's minimum distance is 5, the minimum-Hamming-weight coset leader is **unique** for any error of weight ≤2, so the correction is provably the most-likely codeword, never an ambiguous guess; codewords with ≥3 errors yield a non-zero syndrome that no ≤2-bit flip clears and are **flagged `uncorrectable` and decoded best-effort, not mis-corrected** (a wrong page is worse than a flagged one). New `Result` counters `corrected` / `uncorrectable` surface per-decode data quality. **No confidently-wrong output**: the BCH(31,21) generator (`0x769`) and syndrome arithmetic are the same the package's `Synth` encoder already uses to build valid frames, so the **encoder is the verification oracle** — round-trip tests synth a valid page, flip 1 / 2 / 3 bits per codeword, and confirm 1- and 2-bit errors are recovered exactly (address + message intact) while 3-bit errors are flagged; plus direct `bchCorrect` tests over every single-bit position and a spread of bit-pairs, and a syndrome-zero check on the canonical idle/sync words. A bitstream-path accumulation bug (the per-batch `corrected`/`uncorrectable` counts were dropped in `walkBitStream`) was **caught by the end-to-end test** before shipping. Fuzz-clean (~1M execs, 0 crashes); race-clean; lint-clean. Existing decode tests were migrated to **BCH-valid** codewords (the old hand-built helpers zeroed the check bits) so the suite is now protocol-faithful. No new tool — hardens `subghz_pocsag_decode` (`internal/pocsag`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` Intertechno V3 protocol — ✅ shipped v0.662.0 — added the **Intertechno V3** 32/36-bit OOK protocol to `subghz_classify` (now **36 protocols**) — **one of the most widely deployed 433.92 MHz home-automation remote protocols** (Intertechno / CoCo / Elro / KlikAanKlikUit-compatible switches, sockets, dimmers), so a Flipper operator in a smart-home environment will encounter it. Decodes the **32-bit** standard frame (serial = `code>>6` (26-bit), all-channels = `(code>>5)&1`, on/off = `(code>>4)&1`, channel = `~code & 0xF`) and the **36-bit dimming** frame (serial = `code>>10`, dimm_level = `code&0xF`, channel = `~(code>>4)&0xF`). It uses a **distinctive four-phase per-bit encoding** (each data bit is two mark/space pairs; the first space selects the value — `5T`→1, `T`→0), anchored on the start bit (mark T + space 10T, te_short 275µs / te_long 1375µs); the frame ends on a ≥11T space. **Crucially, that four-phase encoding makes Intertechno cleanly distinguishable from the simple-PWM gate/garage decoders — no classifier collision** (the classifier-integration test confirms an Intertechno frame surfaces Intertechno V3 as the top match). This is the deciding property that made Intertechno shippable where the gate-less fixed-code candidates (e.g. Dickert MAHS) were not — those collided with `Gate TX`/`SecplusV1`'s gate-less readers and were correctly **not shipped** (a wrong top-match is worse than a missing one). **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the four-phase decode, the start/stop framing and the 32/36-bit field split are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/intertechno_v3.c` — the `feed` state machine and `check_remote_controller`); a frame that decodes to neither 32 nor 36 bits is **rejected**. **Anchored to BOTH the firmware's documented worked examples** — the 32-bit `Key:0x3F86C59F` (→ all_ch 0, on/off 1, channel 0) and the 36-bit `Key:0x42D2E8856` (→ all_ch 0, channel 0xA, dimm_level 6) — decoded from built pulses with the field breakdown matching the firmware's own comments, plus a 32-bit round-trip across a spread of codes and sync / wrong-bit-count rejections; codes held as uint64; race-clean. No new tool — extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` Marantec24 protocol — ✅ shipped v0.661.0 — added the **Marantec24** 24-bit fixed-code OOK/PWM protocol to `subghz_classify` (now **35 protocols**) — the 24-bit Marantec garage-door remote variant (distinct from the in-tree 12-bit Marantec), common on **European garage doors**. Decodes the 24-bit code into the **20-bit serial** (`code>>4`) and **4-bit button** (`code&0xF`). PWM at te_short 800µs / te_long 1600µs (= 2×te_short, te_delta 200µs), synced on a **9×te_long (~14400µs) inter-frame gap** (the final bit's space is that gap); the **mark length alone selects the bit** — te_long (1600µs) → 0, te_short (800µs) → 1 (bit 0 = long mark + 3×te_short space, bit 1 = short mark + 2×te_long space). **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the PWM encoding and the serial/button split are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/marantec24.c` — the `feed` state machine with its gap-sync + per-bit mark classification and last-bit-closed-by-gap handling, plus `check_remote_controller`: serial = data>>4, btn = data&0xF). Marantec24 carries **no checksum**, so a frame is gated by the gap sync, the 24-bit count and the per-bit PWM timing; its distinctive ~14400µs gap + te keep it from colliding with the other decoders (the classifier-integration test confirms a Marantec24 frame surfaces Marantec24 as the top match). Verified by an encode↔decode round-trip across a spread of serial/button values (incl. all-zero / all-ones / boundary) with the serial/button split cross-checked, plus sync-gap and truncation rejections; the 24-bit code is held as uint64; race-clean. No new tool — extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` Dooya protocol — ✅ shipped v0.660.0 — added the **Dooya** 40-bit fixed-code OOK/PWM protocol to `subghz_classify` (now **34 protocols**), the dominant motor/remote brand for **powered window coverings** (blinds / shutters / curtains, sold under many smart-home labels) — a real physical-access target in modern buildings, extending the Sub-GHz coverage beyond garage/gate into motorised-covering remotes. Decodes the 40-bit code into the **24-bit serial** (`code>>16`), the **channel mode** (`(code>>12)&0xF` — 0 single / 1 multi), the **channel** (`(code>>8)&0xF`), and the **8-bit key** mapped to its named action (long/short press up/down, stop, up+down, up+stop). PWM at te_short 366µs / te_long 733µs (= 2×te_short, te_delta 120µs): bit 0 = short mark + long space, bit 1 = long mark + short space; a **13×te_short (~4758µs) guard mark + 2×te_long space** precedes the 40 bits. **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the PWM encoding and the serial/channel/key split are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/dooya.c` — the `feed` state machine, `get_upload` encoder, and the documented `check_remote_controller` field split + key table). Dooya carries **no checksum**, so a frame is gated by the guard sync, the 40-bit count and the per-bit PWM timing; the specific ~4758µs header + te distinguish it from the gate-less 40-bit SecplusV1 reader (the classifier-integration test confirms a Dooya frame surfaces Dooya as the top match, no collision). **Anchored to the firmware's own documented worked example** — `0xE1DC030533` → serial `0xE1DC03`, single channel, channel 5, key `0x33` = "long press down" — plus a full key-table round-trip and sync/truncation rejections; the 40-bit code is held as uint64; race-clean. No new tool — extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` Hormann HSM protocol — ✅ shipped v0.659.0 — added the **Hörmann HSM** 44-bit fixed-code OOK/PWM protocol to `subghz_classify` (now **33 protocols**), one of the **most common European garage-door / gate brands** — a genuine high-value gap in the project's core Sub-GHz remote-cloning surface. Decodes the 44-bit code and the **4-bit button** (`code>>8 & 0xF`). PWM at te_short 500µs / te_long 1000µs (= 2×te_short, te_delta 200µs): bit 0 = short mark + long space, bit 1 = long mark + short space; a **24×te_short (~12000µs) guard mark + te_short space** precedes (and a repeat terminates) the frame, and the mark length selects each bit. **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the PWM encoding, the **fixed-pattern gate** and the button split are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/hormann.c` — `te_short=500`, `te_long=1000`, `min_count_bit_for_found=44`, `HORMANN_HSM_PATTERN=0xFF000000003`; the `feed` state machine, `get_upload` encoder, and the `check()` pattern gate + `btn` split). Hörmann HSM carries **no rolling code or CRC**, so a frame is gated by the guard sync, the 44-bit count, the per-bit PWM timing, **and the fixed-pattern bits** — every valid HSM code has the top 8 + bottom 2 bits set, so a 44-bit frame failing `(code & 0xFF000000003) == 0xFF000000003` is **rejected, not mis-identified**. Because `SecplusV1`'s gate-less 40-bit rolling-code reader also accepts a Hörmann frame's 40-bit prefix (a pre-existing looseness — Security+ v1 has no checksum to gate on), Hörmann is **ordered before SecplusV1** in the classifier so its strict, specific pattern gate **wins the confidence tie** for genuine Hörmann frames; SecplusV1 still classifies its own frames correctly (Hörmann's 44-bit/guard/pattern gate never matches them). Verified by a decode round-trip across pattern-valid codes / every button, the **pattern-gate rejection** of a frame missing the fixed bits, a no-sync rejection, and a **classifier-integration test** confirming a Hörmann frame surfaces Hörmann as the top match; the 44-bit code is held as uint64; race-clean. No new tool — extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` GangQi protocol — ✅ shipped v0.633.0 — added the **GangQi** 34-bit OOK/PWM protocol to `subghz_classify` (now 32 protocols), the Chinese alarm/gate/barrier-remote format added to the Flipper firmware 09.2024. Decodes the 34-bit code, the **20-bit serial** (`code>>16 & 0xFFFFF`), the **4-bit button** (`code>>10 & 0xF`, named per the firmware's button table — Arm / Disarm / Alarm / Ring / settings), and the **8-bit bytesum** (`code>>2 & 0xFF`). PWM at te_short 500µs / te_long 1200µs (te_delta 200µs): bit 0 = short mark + long space, bit 1 = long mark + short space; a 2×te_long (~2400µs) inter-frame GAP both precedes the first bit and terminates the frame — the final bit's trailing space is that gap, from which the firmware derives the last bit's value. **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the PWM encoding, the field split and the **additive bytesum** are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/gangqi.c` — the `feed` state machine, `get_upload` encoder, and `get_string`'s two accepted sums: the original-remote form `0xC8 − serial_hi − serial_lo − (0xD0|btn)` and the "backdoor" form `0x02 + serial_hi + serial_lo + (0xD0|btn)`, computed in 8-bit arithmetic). The bytesum is a **soft gate**: a frame whose checksum matches neither sum still decodes but is **confidence-halved and flagged** (`checksum_ok:false`), so a checksum-valid match always outranks it — never asserted as a real credential. Verified by a decode round-trip across a spread of codes built with firmware-correct bytesums (incl. all-zero / all-ones / each named button), a corrupted-checksum case (decodes at 0.5 confidence, flagged), and sync-gap / truncation rejections; the 34-bit code is held as uint64. Race-clean. This release also corrects a docs/code drift — the tool Description and package doc had fallen behind at "28"/"20" protocols while the classifier already carried 31; both now read 32. No new tool — extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` Mastercode protocol — ✅ shipped v0.632.0 — added the **Mastercode** 36-bit OOK/PWM gate/barrier-remote protocol to `subghz_classify` (now 31 protocols). Decodes the 36-bit code, the **16-bit serial** (`code>>4 & 0xFFFF`, eight tri-state DIP positions) and the **2-bit button** (`code>>2 & 0x03`). PWM at te_short 1072µs / te_long 2145µs: bit 0 = short mark + long space, bit 1 = long mark + short space; a ~15×te_short inter-frame gap both precedes and terminates the frame, and the mark length selects each bit. **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the PWM encoding and the serial/button split are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/mastercode.c` — the `feed` state machine, `get_upload` encoder and `check_remote_controller`). Mastercode carries **no checksum**, so a frame is gated only by the sync gap, the 36-bit count and the per-bit PWM timing — the classifier ranks it against other matches by confidence. Verified by a decode round-trip across a spread of 36-bit codes (including all-zero / all-ones / boundary values) plus sync-gap and truncation rejections; the 36-bit code is held as uint64. Race-clean. No new tool — extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` Magellan protocol — ✅ shipped v0.631.0 — added the **Magellan** 32-bit OOK/PWM protocol to `subghz_classify` (now 30 protocols), broadening coverage into **security-system sensors/remotes** (door/motion/smoke/REM events) rather than only garage remotes. Frame: 24-bit data + 8-bit CRC8; the 24-bit data, **bit-reversed**, splits into an 8-bit event code and a 16-bit serial. PWM: bit 1 = te_short mark + te_long space, bit 0 = te_long mark + te_short space (te_short 200µs / te_long 400µs); a te_long×3 start mark anchors the frame after a ~12×te_short preamble. **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the PWM encoding, the CRC-8 (poly 0x31, init 0x00 over the three data bytes) and the reverse-then-split field formula are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/magellan.c` — the `feed` state machine, `get_upload` encoder, `magellan_crc8`/`check_crc` and `check_remote_controller`); a frame failing the **CRC-8 gate is rejected**, never surfaced. Verified against the **firmware's own documented example** (0x37AE4828 → CRC 0x28, reversed 0x1275EC → event 0x12, serial 0x75EC) — the CRC port is pinned by that vector independently — plus a decode round-trip across a spread of event/serial values and CRC-mismatch / truncated / no-start-bit rejections; race-clean. No new tool — extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` MegaCode protocol — ✅ shipped v0.629.0 — added the **Linear MegaCode** 24-bit fixed-code OOK protocol to `subghz_classify` (now 29 protocols). MegaCode is the Linear/Nortek garage/gate remote format (315 MHz AM). Decodes the 24-bit static code and the **4-bit facility code + 16-bit serial/key + 3-bit button** field split, with the **start bit (MSB) required to be 1** as a structural gate. The on-air encoding is pulse-position within a fixed 6×TE frame, which collapses to a constant 1×TE mark separated by an inter-mark space whose width encodes the (prev,cur) bit pair — (1,1)=5×TE, (1,0)=2×TE, (0,1)=8×TE, (0,0)=5×TE; the decoder normalises this by subtracting 3×TE from the space when the previous bit was 0, then classifies 5×TE→1 / 2×TE→0, exactly as the firmware does. A leading guard space of 11–14×TE precedes the frame; a space ≥10×TE ends it. **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings (te=1000µs), the space-to-bit normalisation and the facility/serial/button split are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/megacode.c` — the `feed` decoder state machine, the `get_upload` encoder gap widths, and `check_remote_controller`); the gap table is **cross-checked between two independent firmware functions** (decoder + encoder agree), and a frame whose start bit is not 1 is **rejected**. Verified against the **worked example documented verbatim in the firmware** (remote key 17316 / facility 3 / button 1 → 0x9A1D21) plus a decode round-trip across a deterministic spread of facility/serial/button values and structural-rejection cases; race-clean. No new tool — extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` SMC5326 protocol — ✅ shipped v0.628.0 — added the **SMC5326** (PT2262-family tri-state encoder) 25-bit fixed-code OOK/PWM protocol to `subghz_classify` (now 28 protocols). SMC5326 is a standard PT2262-compatible encoder chip in countless cheap remotes / sensors. Decodes the 25-bit code and the **16-bit address** (`code>>9 & 0xFFFF`, eight tri-state DIP positions) per the Flipper reference. Mark-first PWM: bit 0 = short mark + long space, bit 1 = long mark + short space (te_short 300µs / te_long 900µs = 3×TE); frame preceded by a ~24×TE inter-frame gap space. **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the mark-first PWM encoding and the address split are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/smc5326.c` — the `get_upload` encoder + the decoder feed loop + `get_string`); the decoder uses `estimateTEMin` (the short/long pulses appear ~equally per bit). Verified by a decode round-trip over four codes built per the firmware's encoder, address cross-checked (code 0x0123456 → address 0x091A); race-clean. No new tool — extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `subghz_classify` Gate TX protocol — ✅ shipped v0.627.0 — added the **Gate TX** (GateTX) 24-bit fixed-code OOK/PWM Sub-GHz protocol to the `subghz_classify` decoder set (now 27 protocols). Gate TX is a common garage/gate remote format. Decodes the 24-bit code and derives the **20-bit serial + 4-bit button** from the bit-reversed key, per the Flipper reference. Frame: a long header space (~47×TE) + a te_long start-bit mark, then 24 MSB-first PWM bits (bit 0 = short space + long mark, bit 1 = long space + short mark; te_short 350µs / te_long 700µs). **No confidently-wrong output**: the timings, the PWM bit encoding and the serial/button reversed-key formula are taken **verbatim** from the Flipper Zero firmware (`lib/subghz/protocols/gate_tx.c` — the `get_upload` encoder + the `GateTXDecoderStep` state machine + `check_remote_controller`), and the decoder uses `estimateTEMin` (not the naive estimator, which would mis-pick te_long since the short/long pulses appear ~equally per bit). Verified by a decode round-trip over three codes built per the firmware's own encoder, with the serial/button cross-checked against the reversed-key formula (e.g. code 0x123456 → serial 295622 / button 10); race-clean. No new tool — extends `subghz_classify` (`internal/subghz/protocols`); registry unchanged.
- `cyfral_decode` (Cyfral iButton frame) — ✅ shipped v0.626.0 — decodes the **Cyfral** iButton contact-key (former-CIS / Eastern-European intercom systems) — the second of the two **non-Dallas iButton** formats `ibutton_decode` deferred, **completing the iButton family** (Dallas + Metakom + Cyfral). **Takes the on-wire frame, not the rendered 2-byte ID**: a Cyfral key decodes to 16 bits but that value carries no integrity information (every 16-bit value is structurally valid), so the genuine, gated decode is of the 40-bit on-wire frame — a start nibble (0b0001), 8 data nibbles each ∈ {1110,1101,1011,0111} (carrying 2 bits each: E→11/D→10/B→01/7→00), a stop nibble (0b0001) — validating those constraints (a strong ~(4/16)⁸ gate) and extracting the key. **No confidently-wrong output**: the frame structure + nibble mapping are taken from the **Flipper Zero firmware** (`lib/ibutton/protocols/misc/protocol_cyfral.c`); a frame failing any nibble constraint is **rejected** as not-a-Cyfral-frame rather than mis-decoded; the mapping is hand-checkable (no external vector). Verified against a hand-traced vector (on-wire `1EDB7EDB71` → key 0xE4E4), all-0x7/all-0xE extremes, and bad-start / bad-stop / bad-data-nibble / error rejections; fuzz-clean (~3.4M execs, 0 panics). Native — a nibble walk + a 4-entry pattern map, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/cyfral`). Registry 616→617.
- `metakom_decode` (Metakom iButton key) — ✅ shipped v0.625.0 — decodes the **Metakom** 4-byte (32-bit) contact-key format used by Metakom intercom systems (common across the former-CIS / Eastern-European residential market) — one of the two **non-Dallas iButton** formats `ibutton_decode` (Dallas 1-Wire) explicitly deferred (the other is Cyfral). Input is the decoded 4-byte key (the Flipper 'ID' value), MSB-first; the on-wire sync / 0b010 start-stop framing is the reader's job and out of scope, so the decode is deterministic. **No confidently-wrong output**: the key width, byte order and validity rule — every data byte must have an **even** number of 1 bits — are taken from the **Flipper Zero firmware** (`lib/ibutton/protocols/misc/protocol_metakom.c` `metakom_parity_check`), and the rule is hand-checkable by bit-counting (no external vector needed). Metakom carries no stronger structural marker, so the per-byte even parity is the **only** integrity gate (a comparatively weak ~1-in-16 gate) — a key that fails it is reported as parity-invalid rather than asserted as genuine, and the raw bytes are always surfaced. Verified against even-parity-valid (`030F33C3`), odd-parity-invalid (`010F33C3`), all-zero, and error cases; fuzz-clean (~2.5M execs, 0 panics). Native — a 4-byte read + a per-byte even-parity popcount, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/metakom`). Registry 615→616. (Cyfral, the other deferred non-Dallas iButton format, shipped as the follow-up `cyfral_decode` in v0.626.0, completing the iButton family.)
- `ioprox_encode` (IO Prox / Kantech XSF block generator) — ✅ shipped v0.616.0 — the inverse of `ioprox_decode` (v0.608): builds the 64-bit IO Prox (Kantech XSF) LF block from a facility code, version and 16-bit card number, **closing the ioProx reader-cloning loop** alongside `em4100_encode` and `rfid_pacs_encode` (the block is what you would write to a T5577 to clone a Kantech credential for an authorized test). Builds the documented frame (nine zero preamble bits + 0xF0 marker + the six framing separators + facility/version/card) and recomputes the 8-bit checksum (`0xFF - (0xF0 + facility + version + cardHi + cardLo)`) so the emitted block always carries a correct CRC. **No confidently-wrong output**: the layout + checksum are the same Proxmark3-/Flipper-cross-verified ones `ioprox_decode` uses, and the encoder **round-trips** with it (decoding the emitted block reproduces the inputs with a valid CRC) and reproduces the hand-traced reference vector (FC=1 / V=1 / Card=1337 → `007840603059CF3F`) — the strongest verification, no external vector needed. Generation only — transmits nothing and writes to no device, so it stays Low like the decoder. Verified by the hand-vector match and a decode∘encode round-trip across several FC/version/card triples; native — fixed bit placement + an 8-bit checksum, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/ioprox`). Registry 608→609.
- `ioprox_decode` (IO Prox / Kantech XSF 125 kHz LF access-control decode) — ✅ shipped v0.608.0 — decodes the **IO Prox (Kantech XSF)** 64-bit LF data block, the credential format used by **Kantech ioProx** readers (widely deployed across North American commercial / institutional access control) — closing the **LF reader-cloning recon gap** left by the HID Prox / Indala / AWID PACS coverage, and complementing `em4100_decode` / `fdxb_decode`. Recovers the **facility code**, the **version** byte, the **16-bit card number**, and validates the **8-bit checksum** (`0xFF - (0xF0 + FC + V + cardHi + cardLo) mod 256`). Input is the *decoded* 64-bit block — the 'Raw' bytes a Proxmark3 `lf io demod` / Flipper Zero LF read emits, MSB-first; the on-air FSK demodulation is the reader's job and out of scope, so the decode is deterministic. **No confidently-wrong output**: the bit layout (nine zero preamble bits → 0xF0 marker → FC → version → card-hi → card-lo → checksum, each separated by a framing `1` bit) and the checksum algorithm are taken from — and **agree byte-for-byte between two independent reference implementations**, the **Proxmark3** client (`cmdlfio.c`) and the **Flipper Zero firmware** (`lib/lfrfid/protocols/protocol_io_prox_xsf.c`); the structural frame (preamble + 0xF0 marker + the six separator bits) is a hard gate — a block whose marker or separators don't match is **rejected** as not-an-ioProx-frame rather than mis-decoded, and the checksum is surfaced as `crc_valid` — a structurally-valid block that fails the checksum is reported as such, never asserted as a real credential. Verified against an **independently hand-traced** vector (FC=1 / V=1 / Card=1337 → raw `00 78 40 60 30 59 CF 3F`, checksum 0xCF) plus two more generated from the spec layout, a checksum-mismatch case, and bad-marker / non-zero-preamble structural rejections; fuzz-clean (~4.6M execs, 0 panics). Native — fixed bit extraction at known offsets + an 8-bit additive checksum, stdlib only, no new go.mod dep (`internal/ioprox`). Registry 601→602.
- `fdxb_decode` (ISO 11784/11785 FDX-B animal/pet-microchip LF decode) — ✅ shipped v0.464.0 — decodes the **FDX-B data block**, the 134.2 kHz LF transponder format in pet/animal microchips (and many asset/biothermo tags) — the LF complement to the project's EM4100 / HID-Prox / PACS decoders (it read/emulated FDX-B on hardware but had no offline data-block decode). Recovers the **country code** (10-bit LSB-first), the **38-bit national identification number** (LSB-first), the data-block-status and animal-application flags, and validates the **CRC-16** (CCITT poly 0x1021, init 0x0000, refin=false/refout=true, over the 8-byte ID block — the integrity gate). On-air framing (11-bit preamble + control-bit stuffing) is the demodulator's job and out of scope, so the decode is deterministic. The field layout, LSB-first bit order, and CRC-16 parameters are taken from the **Proxmark3 reference** (`common/crc16.c crc16_fdxb` + `client cmdlffdxb.c`) and **verified byte-for-byte against two real decoded tags** — country 528 (Netherlands) / national 140000795552 (raw ID `05 D9 4D 19 04 21 00 01`) and country 999 / national 1500030037 (CRC `0x8A1C`) — not recalled. No confidently-wrong output: a CRC-failed frame is reported as such (never asserted as a real tag), a 900-999 manufacturer/test country code is noted rather than mapped, and the reserved/extended bits are surfaced raw. Verified against both real vectors + CRC-mismatch / extended-block / error cases; fuzz-clean (5.6M execs, 0 panics). Native — fixed bit/byte extraction + CRC-16, stdlib only (`internal/fdxb`).
- NDEF **Connection Handover** records (`Hs` / `Hr` / `ac` / `cr` / `err`) — ✅ shipped v0.463.0 — completes the tap-to-pair / tap-to-connect decode tree in `ndef_decode` (no new tool — recursive NDEF, like Smart Poster). A real handover tag's top-level record is a **Handover Select** (`Hs`) or **Handover Request** (`Hr`): a 1-byte version (major high nibble / minor low) + a nested NDEF message that the decoder now **recurses**, so the **Alternative Carrier** (`ac`) records and the **Wi-Fi WSC / Bluetooth OOB carrier-config records they reference by ID** (shipped v0.461/v0.462) are decoded in place — previously the `Hs` payload was opaque hex and the carriers were never reached. The `ac` record decodes the Carrier Power State (0=inactive / 1=active / 2=activating / 3=unknown), the carrier-data reference (the carrier record's ID), and the auxiliary-data references; `cr` (Collision Resolution) the 2-byte random number; `err` the error-reason byte. Values verified verbatim against the **nfcpy/ndeflib reference** (CPS tuple, `ac` byte layout, version-byte nibbles, `Hs`=version+message) — not recalled. **Also hardened a latent stability bug**: nested-message decode (the pre-existing Smart Poster path and these new handover paths) had **no recursion-depth cap** — a maliciously self-nesting record could exhaust the stack; added a depth=16 guard that leaves the payload raw with a warning past the limit. No confidently-wrong output: reserved error reasons surfaced as `reserved(0xNN)`, truncated `ac` references reported. Verified against a full hand-constructed `Hs → ac → referenced BT-OOB carrier` tree + aux-refs / cr / err / depth-guard cases; fuzz-clean (1.7M execs, 0 panics). Native — recursive descent, stdlib only (`internal/ndef`).
- `bluetooth_oob_decode` (Bluetooth OOB pairing / NFC handover record decode) — ✅ shipped v0.462.0 — decodes the **tap-to-pair** payload: the Bluetooth Secure Simple Pairing OOB data block carried by an NFC handover tag, in both MIME forms — `application/vnd.bluetooth.ep.oob` (BR/EDR "Easy Pairing": a 2-byte little-endian OOB Data Length + 6-byte little-endian BD_ADDR + EIR) and `application/vnd.bluetooth.le.oob` (Bluetooth LE: a bare AD-structure sequence). Recovers the peer's Bluetooth address, device class, LE role, local name, and the SSP OOB key material a tag offers. Both variants run through the **shared `internal/ble` EIR/AD walker**, which this work extended with value decoders for the OOB-critical AD types it previously only named: **LE Role** (0x1C → Peripheral / Central / preferred, per Bluetooth CSS Part A §1.17), **LE Bluetooth Device Address** (0x1B → 6 LE address bytes + public/random type flag), and **Class of Device** (0x0D → 24-bit value + named Major Device Class) — so `ble_gap_decode` benefits too. The BR/EDR framing and the LE value formats are taken **verbatim from the Bluetooth Core Specification Supplement and the NFC Forum "Bluetooth Secure Simple Pairing Using NFC" application document (as implemented in the ndeflib reference)** — verified, not recalled. No confidently-wrong output: the declared OOB length is checked-not-asserted (mismatch noted), reserved LE-role values are surfaced as `reserved(0xNN)`, and the opaque OOB key material (Hash C / Randomizer R / LE SC confirmation+random / SM TK) is left as raw hex.
